RATING: 8
Two player wargame in the "Commands & Colors" series themed around ancient battles (Romans vs. Carthaginians). A combination of card driven mechanics for issuing unit orders and specialized dice to resolve combat are used. Works well despite random elements - demands that players adapt strategies to their cards and use rules to increase odds in their favor to maximize dice roll success. Plays in 1 hour per battle but a proper match will see 2 games being played back-to-back with players switching sides and the winner declared from the total score of the two games. Upgraded my copy with the C&C:A dice from Valley Games, the mounted board from the 2nd expansion, some card holders.

---

Выбрал ССА :)

---

Сыграно 3 партии, наклеены почти все наклейки :) Что я могу сказать про игру. Она играбельна, быстра и интересна. Насколько - пока говорить рано. Но вот что хотелось бы отметить:

1. Я не совсем понимаю зачем было на кубиках делать 3 хита разного цвета. Это осложнило все таблицы, объяснения и броски. Хватило бы одного хита и двух промахов, вместо 3 разных цветов (где хит зависит от цвета юнита, а два других получаются промахами). Ну есть может быть парочка командных карт, где используются цвета, но это того не стоит. Возможно изначально в механике от этого зависело больше, а в итоговом варианте цвета роль потеряли, но остались на кубиках.

2. В игре много рандома. Я не считаю что это плохо. Но особенно важно отметить, что ССА являются именно игрой, а не реконструкцией. Это важно понимать. Чтобы потом не удивляться, почему в реальной истории в такой-то битве был удар правым флангом, а вам вообще тупо не пришла ни одна такая карта.

3. Как бы ни были хороши битвы, без уровня стратегии они будут что-то терять. Например так вам не важно с какими потерями разбить врага. Например в игре "Ганнибал: Рим против Карфагена" огромную роль играет с какими потерями битва закончилась, а не только кто победил (победа может ничего и не дать, или даже быть слишком дорогой). Частично проблема решается более сложными сценариями, но сценарии тоже не безупречны.

4. Не слушайте, что это легкий семейный варгейм. Да, он легкий, но только в сравнении с другими варгеймами. Типичная семейная игра на порядок проще, особенно на этапе входа в игру.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
"Commands & Colors: Ancients depicts warfare from the Dawn of Military History (3000 BC) to the opening of the Middle Ages (400 AD). Quite an ambitious undertaking for one game, yet Commands & Colors by design is a unique historical game system which allows players to effectively portray stylized battles from this time in history. The 15 battles, showcased in the scenario booklet, although stylized, focus on important terrain features and the historical deployment of forces in scale with the game system. The battles include Bagradas, Cannae, and Zama." This is a beautiful game! Expansions: Commands & Colors: Ancients Expansion Pack #1: Greece & Eastern Kingdoms, Commands & Colors: Ancients Expansion Pack #2: Rome and the Barbarians, Commands & Colors: Ancients Expansion Pack #3: The Roman Civil Wars

RATING: 6
Support and battle back are nice additions, and leadership is paramount.  But I'll just never love the core C&C system, with the goofy loss tracking (you have blocks; why not steal a page from Columbia and rotate them?), the very high level of randomness, and the fairly shallow tactics. I also wish there were even more unit types (certainly enough blocks for this, if you don't use the stupid multi-block system), and more hooks for them to have special abilities.  And while I'm complaining, how about smaller hexes and more sense of maneuver?

I like the card dilemmas and managing around that, though, and the randomness can produce dramatic moments.  Also, the theme here is a better fit than in the others (Memoir feels particularly odd on this score; I haven't played BattleLore and don't intend to).

RATING: 9
A solid addition to the C&C line of games. More rich than Memoir '44 or Battle Cry, less confusing than BattleLore -- I'd say it's the best so far. BUT the scenarii are "historically" horribly unbalanced. You need to play more than one game to get revenge. :)

EDIT: I've been playing tons of Ancients with my girlfriend (who knew she had the heart of a wargamer?) and we've found that we didn't really like to play scenarii back and forth--we prefer to forge ahead into History. So what we do to mitigate the frustration factor is that whoever got beat up in the previous game gets to play the side that's "supposed" to win in the next game. This tends to cancel out the historical disadvantages and makes the game less frustrating because we essentially take turns playing the underdog.

RATING: 7.5

Setup and tear down takes some time but the games play quickly. My current feeling is the randomness of the card draw can be effectively balanced by keeping your troops in good locations, keeping coherent groups, and saving some good cards until later in the game. I have the board under plexiglass which helps to keep it flat.

RATING: N/A
Tactical level battle simulation using a mix of cards to drive commands and dice to resolve battle. Complex enough to be interesting but not burdensome for a fairly quick (1-3 hours) game. I like the random element in the game that can cause a good strategy to fail or turn a suicide assault into a game winning offensive. I feel it mimics the reality of fog of war and the unexpected that occur in real battles. The blocks are pleasantly tactile. Rolling dice to resolve battles is eminently satisfying as well.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Best of Borg's designs so far... Good idea to provide mounted boards. Now, if we could only get rid of those blocks! Campaign Book ala Memoir, please?

I substituted blocks with 1/72 scale plastic miniatures, and so far happy with them. I used a simple conversion system where all light cavalry/infantry/auxiliaries have javelins, all mediums have swords, and all heavies have spears - easy to tell them apart at a glance. Romans are gray (Zvezda), Carthaginians are olive (Zvezda/HAT), Persians are red/brown (Zvezda/Caesar) and Greeks are gray or pink (Caesar/Zvezda/HAT). Miniatures look much better then the blocks, but it takes longer to set them up and store them away, plus they take more space.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I like C&C:A. I really like the leadership influence in the command cards and "formations" and the support modifier to reduce the retreat flags during combat. There are a lot of units to wrap your head around, and I constantly had to refer to the player aids to figure out whether a unit could evade, advance after combat, etc. But I could see this becoming pretty familiar after a few plays. I'm not a big fan of the production quality, though -- the blocks are arduous to sticker, sort and store. The map is fairly flimsy and holds the creases so it won't lay flat easily, the card "planks" don't shuffle well and the dice are horrible. I'm a dice fanatic, so ridiculously awful dice like this literally drop my rating down a half point.

RATING: 7.5
This game is a great complement to my 2-player repertoire. It plays in under an hour, and the command cards make players plan ahead or work around an absence of orders for a column or unit type.

My only quibble with the design is that the combat feels a bit too random. The swords and helmets account for superior attack power, but the defenses feel very similar for all units. I won a game that I should have lost by taking 4 banners of a 5 banner objective in the final turn. That the luck factor can decide matches rather than just influence them makes C & C: A just a touch less enjoyable.
